# Searching Sourcegraph

Search before you build. Existing patterns reduce tokens, ensure consistency, and surface tested solutions.

Use `sg_list_repos` to discover available repositories before searching.


## Tool Selection Logic

**Start here:**

1. **Know the exact symbol or pattern?** → `sg_keyword_search`
2. **Know the concept, not the code?** → `sg_nls_search`
3. **Need to understand how/why?** → `sg_deepsearch_read`
4. **Tracing a symbol's usage?** → `sg_find_references`
5. **Need full implementation?** → `sg_go_to_definition` → `sg_read_file`

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Exact code patterns | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Trace usage | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Understand systems | `sg_deepsearch_read` |
| Read files | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
file:.*\.test\.ts$ -file:__mocks__   # Tests, exclude mocks
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

Combine filters: `repo:^github.com/myorg/backend$ file:src/handlers lang:typescript`

## Context-Aware Behaviour

**When the user provides a file path or error message:**
- Extract symbols, function names, or error codes
- Search for those exact terms first
- Trace references if the error involves a known symbol

**When the user asks "how does X work":**
- Prefer `sg_deepsearch_read` for architectural understanding
- Follow up with `sg_read_file` on key files mentioned in the response

**When the user is implementing a new feature:**
- Search for similar existing implementations first
- Read tests for usage examples
- Check for shared utilities before creating new ones

**When debugging:**
- Search for the exact error string
- Trace the symbol where the error is thrown
- Check recent changes with `sg_diff_search`

## Workflows

For detailed step-by-step workflows, see:
- `workflows/implementing-feature.md` — when building new features
- `workflows/understanding-code.md` — when exploring unfamiliar systems
- `workflows/debugging-issue.md` — when tracking down bugs

## Efficiency Rules

**Minimise tool calls:**
- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms (faster, more precise)

**Batch your understanding:**
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than reading one and asking questions
- Use `sg_deepsearch_read` for "how does X work" instead of multiple keyword searches

**Avoid common token waste:**
- Don't search all repos when you know the target repo
- Don't use `sg_deepsearch_read` for simple "find all" queries
- Don't re-read files you've already seen in this conversation

## Query Patterns

| Intent | Query |
|--------|-------|
| React hooks | `file:.*\.tsx$ use[A-Z].*= \(` |
| API routes | `file:src/api app\.(get\|post\|put\|delete)` |
| Error handling | `catch.*Error\|\.catch\(` |
| Type definitions | `file:types/ export (interface\|type)` |
| Test setup | `file:.*\.test\. beforeEach\|beforeAll` |
| Config files | `file:(webpack\|vite\|rollup)\.config` |
| CI/CD | `file:\.github/workflows deploy` |

For more patterns, see `query-patterns.md`.

## Output Formatting

**Search results:**
- Present as a brief summary, not raw tool output
- Highlight the most relevant file and line
- Include a code snippet only if it directly answers the question

**Code explanations:**
- Start with a one-sentence summary
- Use the codebase's own terminology
- Reference specific files and functions

**Recommendations:**
- Present as numbered steps if actionable
- Link to specific patterns found in the codebase
- Note any existing utilities that should be reused

## Common Mistakes

| Mistake | Fix |
|---------|-----|
| Searching all repos | Add `repo:^github.com/org/repo$` |
| Too many results | Add `file:` pattern or keywords |
| Missing relevant code | Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching |
| Not understanding context | Use `sg_deepsearch_read` |
| Guessing patterns | Read implementations with `sg_read_file` |

## Principles

- Start narrow, expand if needed
- Chain tools: search → read → find references → definition
- Check tests for usage examples
- Read before generating

# Task: Kubernetes API Server Architecture and Extension Guide

**Repository:** kubernetes/kubernetes (stripped snapshot)
**Output:** Write your document to `/workspace/documentation.md`

## Objective

Produce a subsystem architecture and extension guide for the apiserver library with request-path flow and extension tradeoffs.

## Scope

Focus on the Kubernetes apiserver library subsystem.
Your document must explain component responsibilities, end-to-end flow, and extension or operational tradeoffs.

## Content Expectations

Address all of the following in your own structure:
- subsystem purpose, boundaries, and upstream/downstream dependencies
- key components and how responsibilities are split
- end-to-end control/request flow with concrete repository evidence
- failure modes, limits, and design tradeoffs
- extension points, customization hooks, and associated risks
- a concise map of the most important files/directories used in your analysis

## Quality Bar

- Cite concrete file paths from the repository.
- Explain behavior and interactions, not just API signatures.
- Include at least one section on operational implications (performance, reliability, or maintainability).
- Do not fabricate classes, functions, or files.

## Anti-Requirements

- Do not output `doc.go`.
- Do not provide shallow bullet dumps without system flow explanation.
- Do not rely on external docs not present in the workspace.

118-assistanttext-
The documentation has been written to `/workspace/documentation.md`. Here is a summary of what it covers:

---

**Section 1 — Purpose, Boundaries, and Dependencies**  
Explains that `k8s.io/apiserver` is the generic API server framework used by all three servers inside `kube-apiserver` and any extension API server. Lists upstream dependencies (apimachinery, client-go, etcd client, kube-openapi) and downstream consumers (kube-aggregator, apiextensions-apiserver, aggregated extension servers).

**Section 2 — Key Components**  
Documents ten distinct components with their responsibilities and the concrete files they live in:
- `Config` / `RecommendedConfig` — server configuration and default values
- `GenericAPIServer` — runtime server struct, lifecycle, delegation chain
- `APIServerHandler` — HTTP handler tree (GoRestful + NonGoRestfulMux Director)
- Authentication, Authorization, Admission Control — pluggable interfaces and union composition
- Endpoints Layer (`APIInstaller`) — REST verb → handler reflection
- Registry Layer (`genericregistry.Store`) — generic CRUD with strategy objects and lifecycle hooks
- Storage Layer (`storage.Interface`, etcd3 implementation) — persistence with optimistic locking
- Watch Cache (`Cacher`, `WatchCache`) — in-memory fan-out layer in front of etcd

**Section 3 — End-to-End Request Flow**  
Traces: server chain delegation → all 25 filter stages of `DefaultBuildHandlerChain` with execution order and security rationale → API group registration pathway → read path (cache-first, etcd fallback) → write path (decode → admit → strategy → `GuaranteedUpdate` CAS loop).

**Section 4 — Failure Modes, Limits, and Tradeoffs**  
Covers: in-flight request limits (APF vs. simple counter), watch cache staleness and bookmark mechanism, optimistic concurr
... (truncated)

{
  "path": "staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/ARCHITECTURE.md",
  "repo": "github.com/kubernetes/kubernetes"

Output
{
  "content": "{\"content\":\"1: # apiserver Architecture\\n2: \\n3: ## 1. Server Composition\\n4: \\n5: The `kube-apiserver` binary is not one server, but a **server chain** of three distinct\\n6: `GenericAPIServer` instances: the core Kubernetes API, API extensions (CRDs), and the aggregation\\n7: layer.\\n8: \\n9: This composition is managed by a layered configuration system, starting with command-line\\n10: flags parsed by `options` structs (e.g., `RecommendedOptions` in `pkg/server/options`), which\\n11: populate a `Config` object that is then used to instantiate the `GenericAPIServer`\\n12: instances. The construction of this delegation chain can be found in the `CreateServerChain`\\n13: function in `cmd/kube-apiserver/app/server.go`.\\n14: \\n15: ```mermaid\\n16: graph TD\\n17:     subgraph Incoming Request\\n18:         direction LR\\n19:         A[User/Client] --> B{/apis/apps/v1/deployments};\\n20:     end\\n21: \\n22:     subgraph kube-apiserver process\\n23:         direction LR\\n24:         B --> C[Aggregator Server];\\n25:         C -- Not an APIService --> D[Kube API Server];\\n26:         D -- Handles Request --> E[REST Storage];\\n27:         C -- Is an APIService --> F[Proxy to Extension API Server];\\n28:         D -- Not a Core API --> G[API Extensions Server];\\n29:         G -- Handles CRD --> E;\\n30:     end\\n31: ```\\n32: \\n33: 1.  **Aggregator Server (`kube-aggregator`):**\\n34:     *   **Purpose:** Handles the `apiregistration.k8s.io` API and acts as a reverse proxy for\\n35:         extension API servers. This functionality was designed to allow third-party APIs to be\\n36:         \\\"aggregated\\\" into the main Kubernetes API server seamlessly.\\n37:     *   **Mechanism:** It watches `APIService` objects. When a request arrives (e.g., for\\n38:         `/apis/mycompany.com/v1/myresources`), it checks if an `APIService` has \\\"claimed\\\"\\n39:         that path. If so, it uses a `ServiceResolver` to find the IP of the backing\\n40:         `Service` and proxies the request.\\n41:     *   **Use Case:** This pattern is for programmatic, high-control extensions that require\\n42:         custom business logic (e.g., non-CRUD subresources like `/logs`) or alternative\\n43:         storage backends.\\n44:     *   **Delegation:** If no `APIService` matches, it delegates the request to the next\\n45:         server in the chain.\\n46: \\n47: 2.  **Kube API Server (Core):**\\n48:     *   **Purpose:** Serves all the built-in Kubernetes APIs (`core/v1`, `apps/v1`, etc.).\\n49:     *   **Mechanism:** This is the main server, configured with all the core REST storage\\n50:         strategies.\\n51:     *   **Delegation:** If a request is for a path that is not a core API (e.g., for a CRD),\\n52:         it delegates the request to the next server in the chain.\\n53: \\n54: 3.  **API Extensions Server (`apiextensions-apiserver`):**\\n55:     *   **Purpose:** Handles the `apiextensions.k8s.io` API, which manages\\n56:         `CustomResourceDefinition` objects (CRDs). The evolution of CRDs from a simple extension\\n57:         mechanism to a feature-rich system with validation, versioning, and defaulting is\\n58:         documented in a series of KEPs, starting with the graduation to GA in Kubernetes v1.16.\\n59:     *   **Mechanism:** When a CRD is created, this server dynamically creates and installs a\\n60:         new REST storage handler for the new resource, making it immediately available.\\n61:     *   **Use Case:** CRDs are the most common extension pattern, offering a declarative,\\n62:         schema-based way to define new resource types that are stored in etcd and require no\\n63:         custom API server code.\\n64:     *   **Delegation:** It is the end of the chain. If it cannot handle a request, a `404 Not\\n65:         Found` is returned.\\n66: \\n67: ## 2. Handler Chain\\n68: \\n69: Every request flows through a standard chain of HTTP handlers (filters). The request body\\n70: is not deserialized until it has passed authentication and authorization. The default handler\\n71: chain is constructed by the `DefaultBuildHandlerChain` function in\\n72: `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/server/config.go`.\\n73: \\n74: ```mermaid\\n75: sequenceDiagram\\n76:     participant Client\\n77:     participant Handler Chain\\n78:     participant Authentication\\n79:     participant Authorization\\n80:     participant Priority and Fairness\\n81:     participant Admission Control\\n82:     participant REST Endpoint\\n83: \\n84:     Client->>Handler Chain: Request\\n85:     Handler Chain->>Authentication: Authenticate\\n86:     Authentication-->>Handler Chain: User Info\\n87:     Handler Chain->>Authorization: Authorize\\n88:     Authorization-->>Handler Chain: Allowed/Denied\\n89:     Handler Chain->>Priority and Fairness: Classify & Queue\\n90:     Priority and Fairness-->>Handler Chain: Proceed\\n91:     Handler Chain->>Admission Control: Mutate & Validate\\n92:     Admission Control-->>Handler Chain: Object OK\\n93:     Handler Chain->>REST Endpoint: Handle\\n94:     REST Endpoint-->>Handler Chain: Response\\n95:     Handler Chain-->>Client: Response\\n96: ```\\n97: \\n98: The handler chain consists of the following stages:\\n99: \\n100: 1.  **Authentication (`pkg/authentication`):** This filter identifies the user. The system is\\n101:     pluggable and composed of multiple authenticators (e.g., client certs, bearer tokens, OIDC).\\n102:     The identity of the user is determined by the first authenticator in the chain that successfully\\n103:     identifies the user.\\n104: 2.  **Authorization (`pkg/authorization`):** This filter checks if the user is permitted to\\n105:     perform the action. This system is also pluggable and composed of multiple authorizers\\n106:     (e.g., RBAC, Node, Webhook). Each authorizer may respond with either allow, deny, or no opinion.\\n107:     If the response is no opinion, the request is passed to the next authorizer in the chain.\\n108: 3.  **Priority and Fairness (`pkg/util/flowcontrol`):** This subsystem manages request\\n109:     concurrency, classifying requests into `FlowSchema`s and `PriorityLevel`s to prevent\\n110:     overload. This feature was introduced to prevent high traffic from overwhelming the API\\n111:     server and to ensure that critical cluster operations are not starved.\\n112: 4.  **Admission Control (`pkg/admission`):** This is the primary mechanism for policy\\n113:     enforcement. It is only at this stage that the request body is deserialized into an\\n114:     object. It is a chain of plugins that can mutate or validate an object. The built-in Pod\\n115:     Security admission controller is a key example of this, enforcing Pod Security Standards\\n116:     at the namespace level.\\n117: 5.  **REST Endpoint Handling (`pkg/endpoints`):** The request is finally dispatched to the\\n118:     appropriate REST handler, which is installed by the `APIInstaller`.\\n119: \\n120: ## 3. API Group Registration\\n121: \\n122: The high-level steps for introducing an API are:\\n123: \\n124: 1.  **Define Types:** Create or modify the Go structs in the `types.go` file for the API group.\\n125: 2.  **Generate Code:** Use the code generators provided by the Kubernetes project to create the required\\n126:     boilerplate methods for deep-copy, conversion, and defaulting.\\n127: 3.  **Implement the `Strategy`:** Write the custom business logic and validation for the\\n128:     resource in its `Strategy` object.\\n129: 4.  **Register and Install:** Create the `APIGroupInfo` struct, bundling the `Scheme` and the\\n130:     `Strategy`-configured storage, and pass it to the `GenericAPIServer`'s `InstallAPIGroup`\\n131:     method.\\n132: \\n133: ### The API Group Registry\\n134: \\n135: The `runtime.Scheme` acts as a central registry for an API group's type information. A single\\n136: `Scheme` object is created for each API group and is responsible for the following key\\n137: capabilities:\\n138: \\n139: *   **Type Registration and Mapping:** The `Scheme`'s primary role is to map a GroupVersionKind\\n140:     (GVK) to its corresponding Go type and back. This process also relies on the `deepcopy-gen`\\n141:     tool to create `DeepCopy()` methods for each type, which is critical for ensuring that\\n142:     objects returned from caches are never modified directly.\\n143: \\n144: *   **API Conversion:** The `Scheme` stores the conversion functions that translate objects\\n145:     between different API versions. These functions are typically generated by the\\n146:     `conversion-gen` tool and enable the **hub-and-spoke** model.\\n147: \\n148: *   **Defaulting:** The `Scheme` registers defaulting functions that populate optional fields in\\n149:     an object. These are usually generated by the `defaulter-gen` tool.\\n150: \\n151: *   **Declarative Validation:** The `Scheme` can store and execute code-generated validation\\n152:     functions, providing a baseline level of validation. This is distinct from the primary,\\n153:     handwritten business logic validation, which is handled by the `Strategy` object.\\n154: \\n155: ### The `APIGroupInfo` Struct and `Strategy` Object\\n156: \\n157: With a populated `Scheme`, the API group is registered with the `GenericAPIServer` by bundling\\n158: the `Scheme` with the storage backend and versioning information into an `APIGroupInfo` struct.\\n159: \\n160: ```mermaid\\n161: graph TD\\n162:     subgraph Server Configuration\\n163:         A[APIGroupInfo for apps v1];\\n164:         A --> B{Scheme: Knows Deployment v1};\\n165:         A --> C{Storage: deployments RESTStorage};\\n166:         A --> D{Version Priority: v1, v1beta1};\\n167:     end\\n168: \\n169:     subgraph RESTStorage Implementation\\n170:         C --> E[genericregistry.Store];\\n171:         E --> F[etcd client];\\n172:         E --> G[Deployment Strategy];\\n173:     end\\n174: \\n175:     subgraph Server Runtime\\n176:         H[GenericAPIServer] -- InstallAPIGroup --> I[APIInstaller];\\n177:         I -- Uses --> A;\\n178:         I --> J{Register /apis/apps/v1/deployments};\\n179:         J --> K[HTTP Handler];\\n180:         K -- On Request --> C;\\n181:     end\\n182: ```\\n183: \\n184: The registration process follows these steps:\\n185: \\n186: 1.  **`APIGroupInfo` Construction:** For each API group, an `APIGroupInfo` struct is created,\\n187:     which contains the populated `Scheme`, a map of resources to their storage\\n188:     implementations, and an ordered list of **Version Priority**.\\n189: \\n190: 2.  **REST Storage Instantiation:** For each resource, a `genericregistry.Store` is created. It\\n191:     is configured with a resource-specific `Strategy` object that contains the core business\\n192:     logic (e.g., handwritten validation).\\n193: \\n194: 3.  **API Group Installation:** The `GenericAPIServer`'s `InstallAPIGroup` method takes the\\n195:     `APIGroupInfo` and uses an `APIInstaller` to expose the resources as HTTP endpoints.\\n196: \\n197: ## 4. Watch Cache\\n198: \\n199: To handle the high volume of watch requests from controllers without overwhelming etcd, the\\n200: apiserver uses a **watch cache**. The implementation can be found in\\n201: `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/storage/cacher/`.\\n202: \\n203: *   **Initialization:** The cacher first performs a `LIST` to get the current state of all\\n204:     objects and a `ResourceVersion` for that point-in-time. It then starts a `WATCH` from\\n205:     that version to ensure a consistent stream of events.\\n206: *   **Serving from Cache:** Most list and watch requests are served from this in-memory cache, which\\n207:     dramatically reduces the load on etcd. Consistent reads are also served from the\\n208:     cache. This is achieved by first fetching the revision number of the latest write from\\n209:     etcd. The server then ensures the cache is at least that recent\u2014waiting for it to\\n210:     refresh if necessary\u2014before serving the request.\\n211: *   **Fallback to Storage:** If a client request cannot be served from the\\n212:     cache's buffer, the request \\\"falls through\\\" to the underlying etcd storage.\\n213: *   **Bookmarks:** The cacher uses bookmark events to track the latest `ResourceVersion` for\\n214:     unchanged objects. This prevents the cache's `ResourceVersion` from becoming too old,\\n215:     which avoids the need for expensive relist operations from etcd when the objects have\\n216:     not been modified.\\n217: \\n218: ## 5. Conflict Resolution\\n219: \\n220: *   **Optimistic Concurrency via `resourceVersion`:** Clients are expected to perform updates using a\\n221:     read-modify-write workflow. The apiserver uses the `resourceVersion` field of every\\n222:     object to enforce optimistic concurrency. This `resourceVersion` is not an arbitrary number;\\n223:     it maps directly to etcd's globally consistent `mod_revision`. When a client submits an\\n224:     update (`PUT` or `PATCH`), it must provide the `resourceVersion` of the object it based its\\n225:     modifications on. If the `resourceVersion` on the server does not match the current\\n226:     `mod_revision` in etcd, the server rejects the request with a `409 Conflict` error. This\\n227:     forces the client to re-read the object, resolve the conflict, and resubmit with the new\\n228:     `resourceVersion`.\\n229: *   **Server-Side Apply:** A declarative, \\\"intent-based\\\" patch. The server maintains a\\n230:     `managedFields` section in the object's metadata to track which \\\"manager\\\" (e.g., a\\n231:     controller) owns each field. This allows multiple actors to manage different parts of the\\n232:     same object without overwriting each other's changes.\\n233: \\n234: ## 6. Discovery and OpenAPI\\n235: \\n236: Apiservers serve the `/apis` discovery endpoints and the `/openapi/v2` and `/openapi/v3`\\n237: specifications. The generation of the OpenAPI specification is a multi-stage process.\\n238: \\n239: *   **`openapi-gen`**: This tool reflects on Go structs, reads godoc comments, and looks at\\n240:     validation struct tags to generate a map of all API definitions.\\n241: *   **`zz_generated.openapi.go`**: The output is a large Go file containing a\\n242:     `GetOpenAPIDefinitions` function.\\n243: *   **Runtime**: The `GenericAPIServer` calls this generated function to build the final OpenAPI\\n244:     JSON spec that it serves to clients.\\n245: \\n246: ## 7. Security & Observability\\n247: \\n248: *   **Audit (`pkg/audit`):** The apiserver has a policy-driven event logging pipeline. The audit\\n249:     policy controls what is logged and at which stage of a request.\\n250: *   **Security:**\\n251:     *   **mTLS:** The primary authentication mechanism for system components.\\n252:     *   **Service Account Token Issuance:** The `kube-apiserver` acts as an OIDC provider,\\n253:         issuing and validating JWTs for `ServiceAccount`s.\\n254: \\n255: ## 8. Streaming Protocols\\n256: \\n257: *   **Websockets:** The apiserver uses websockets to upgrade HTTP\\n258:     connections for interactive, streaming protocols like `exec`, `attach`, and\\n259:     `port-forward`. The `UpgradeAwareProxyHandler` manages this process.\\n260: \",\"url\":\"https://sourcegraph.sourcegraph.com/github.com/kubernetes/kubernetes@b08fa0cdf18610be74d9741cf361446a5f42ff76/-/blob/staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/ARCHITECTURE.md\"}",
  "structuredContent": {
    "content": "1: # apiserver Architecture\n2: \n3: ## 1. Server Composition\n4: \n5: The `kube-apiserver` binary is not one server, but a **server chain** of three distinct\n6: `GenericAPIServer` instances: the core Kubernetes API, API extensions (CRDs), and the aggregation\n7: layer.\n8: \n9: This composition is managed by a layered configuration system, starting with command-line\n10: flags parsed by `options` structs (e.g., `RecommendedOptions` in `pkg/server/options`), which\n11: populate a `Config` object that is then used to instantiate the `GenericAPIServer`\n12: instances. The construction of this delegation chain can be found in the `CreateServerChain`\n13: function in `cmd/kube-apiserver/app/server.go`.\n14: \n15: ```mermaid\n16: graph TD\n17:     subgraph Incoming Request\n18:         direction LR\n19:         A[User/Client] --> B{/apis/apps/v1/deployments};\n20:     end\n21: \n22:     subgraph kube-apiserver process\n23:         direction LR\n24:         B --> C[Aggregator Server];\n25:         C -- Not an APIService --> D[Kube API Server];\n26:         D -- Handles Request --> E[REST Storage];\n27:         C -- Is an APIService --> F[Proxy to Extension API Server];\n28:         D -- Not a Core API --> G[API Extensions Server];\n29:         G -- Handles CRD --> E;\n30:     end\n31: ```\n32: \n33: 1.  **Aggregator Server (`kube-aggregator`):**\n34:     *   **Purpose:** Handles the `apiregistration.k8s.io` API and acts as a reverse proxy for\n35:         extension API servers. This functionality was designed to allow third-party APIs to be\n36:         \"aggregated\" into the main Kubernetes API server seamlessly.\n37:     *   **Mechanism:** It watches `APIService` objects. When a request arrives (e.g., for\n38:         `/apis/mycompany.com/v1/myresources`), it checks if an `APIService` has \"claimed\"\n39:         that path. If so, it uses a `ServiceResolver` to find the IP of the backing\n40:         `Service` and proxies the request.\n41:     *   **Use Case:** This pattern is for programmatic, high-control extensions that require\n42:         custom business logic (e.g., non-CRUD subresources like `/logs`) or alternative\n43:         storage backends.\n44:     *   **Delegation:** If no `APIService` matches, it delegates the request to the next\n45:         server in the chain.\n46: \n47: 2.  **Kube API Server (Core):**\n48:     *   **Purpose:** Serves all the built-in Kubernetes APIs (`core/v1`, `apps/v1`, etc.).\n49:     *   **Mechanism:** This is the main server, configured with all the core REST storage\n50:         strategies.\n51:     *   **Delegation:** If a request is for a path that is not a core API (e.g., for a CRD),\n52:         it delegates the request to the next server in the chain.\n53: \n54: 3.  **API Extensions Server (`apiextensions-apiserver`):**\n55:     *   **Purpose:** Handles the `apiextensions.k8s.io` API, which manages\n56:         `CustomResourceDefinition` objects (CRDs). The evolution of CRDs from a simple extension\n57:         mechanism to a feature-rich system with validation, versioning, and defaulting is\n58:         documented in a series of KEPs, starting with the graduation to GA in Kubernetes v1.16.\n59:     *   **Mechanism:** When a CRD is created, this server dynamically creates and installs a\n60:         new REST storage handler for the new resource, making it immediately available.\n61:     *   **Use Case:** CRDs are the most common extension pattern, offering a declarative,\n62:         schema-based way to define new resource types that are stored in etcd and require no\n63:         custom API server code.\n64:     *   **Delegation:** It is the end of the chain. If it cannot handle a request, a `404 Not\n65:         Found` is returned.\n66: \n67: ## 2. Handler Chain\n68: \n69: Every request flows through a standard chain of HTTP handlers (filters). The request body\n70: is not deserialized until it has passed authentication and authorization. The default handler\n71: chain is constructed by the `DefaultBuildHandlerChain` function in\n72: `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/server/config.go`.\n73: \n74: ```mermaid\n75: sequenceDiagram\n76:     participant Client\n77:     participant Handler Chain\n78:     participant Authentication\n79:     participant Authorization\n80:     participant Priority and Fairness\n81:     participant Admission Control\n82:     participant REST Endpoint\n83: \n84:     Client->>Handler Chain: Request\n85:     Handler Chain->>Authentication: Authenticate\n86:     Authentication-->>Handler Chain: User Info\n87:     Handler Chain->>Authorization: Authorize\n88:     Authorization-->>Handler Chain: Allowed/Denied\n89:     Handler Chain->>Priority and Fairness: Classify & Queue\n90:     Priority and Fairness-->>Handler Chain: Proceed\n91:     Handler Chain->>Admission Control: Mutate & Validate\n92:     Admission Control-->>Handler Chain: Object OK\n93:     Handler Chain->>REST Endpoint: Handle\n94:     REST Endpoint-->>Handler Chain: Response\n95:     Handler Chain-->>Client: Response\n96: ```\n97: \n98: The handler chain consists of the following stages:\n99: \n100: 1.  **Authentication (`pkg/authentication`):** This filter identifies the user. The system is\n101:     pluggable and composed of multiple authenticators (e.g., client certs, bearer tokens, OIDC).\n102:     The identity of the user is determined by the first authenticator in the chain that successfully\n103:     identifies the user.\n104: 2.  **Authorization (`pkg/authorization`):** This filter checks if the user is permitted to\n105:     perform the action. This system is also pluggable and composed of multiple authorizers\n106:     (e.g., RBAC, Node, Webhook). Each authorizer may respond with either allow, deny, or no opinion.\n107:     If the response is no opinion, the request is passed to the next authorizer in the chain.\n108: 3.  **Priority and Fairness (`pkg/util/flowcontrol`):** This subsystem manages request\n109:     concurrency, classifying requests into `FlowSchema`s and `PriorityLevel`s to prevent\n110:     overload. This feature was introduced to prevent high traffic from overwhelming the API\n111:     server and to ensure that critical cluster operations are not starved.\n112: 4.  **Admission Control (`pkg/admission`):** This is the primary mechanism for policy\n113:     enforcement. It is only at this stage that the request body is deserialized into an\n114:     object. It is a chain of plugins that can mutate or validate an object. The built-in Pod\n115:     Security admission controller is a key example of this, enforcing Pod Security Standards\n116:     at the namespace level.\n117: 5.  **REST Endpoint Handling (`pkg/endpoints`):** The request is finally dispatched to the\n118:     appropriate REST handler, which is installed by the `APIInstaller`.\n119: \n120: ## 3. API Group Registration\n121: \n122: The high-level steps for introducing an API are:\n123: \n124: 1.  **Define Types:** Create or modify the Go structs in the `types.go` file for the API group.\n125: 2.  **Generate Code:** Use the code generators provided by the Kubernetes project to create the required\n126:     boilerplate methods for deep-copy, conversion, and defaulting.\n127: 3.  **Implement the `Strategy`:** Write the custom business logic and validation for the\n128:     resource in its `Strategy` object.\n129: 4.  **Register and Install:** Create the `APIGroupInfo` struct, bundling the `Scheme` and the\n130:     `Strategy`-configured storage, and pass it to the `GenericAPIServer`'s `InstallAPIGroup`\n131:     method.\n132: \n133: ### The API Group Registry\n134: \n135: The `runtime.Scheme` acts as a central registry for an API group's type information. A single\n136: `Scheme` object is created for each API group and is responsible for the following key\n137: capabilities:\n138: \n139: *   **Type Registration and Mapping:** The `Scheme`'s primary role is to map a GroupVersionKind\n140:     (GVK) to its corresponding Go type and back. These functions are typically generated by the\n146:     `conversion-gen` tool and enable the **hub-and-spoke** model.\n147: \n148: *   **Defaulting:** The `Scheme` registers defaulting functions that populate optional fields in\n149:     an object. These are usually generated by the `defaulter-gen` tool.\n150: \n151: *   **Declarative Validation:** The `Scheme` can store and execute code-generated validation\n152:     functions, providing a baseline level of validation. Watch Cache\n198: \n199: To handle the high volume of watch requests from controllers without overwhelming etcd, the\n200: apiserver uses a **watch cache**. On a CREATE operation, the client\\n33: \\t// may omit name and rely on the server to generate the name.  If that is the case, this method will return\\n34: \\t// the empty string\\n35: \\tGetName() string\\n36: \\t// GetNamespace is the namespace associated with the request (if any)\\n37: \\tGetNamespace() string\\n38: \\t// GetResource is the name of the resource being requested.  This is not the kind.  For example: pods\\n39: \\tGetResource() schema.GroupVersionResource\\n40: \\t// GetSubresource is the name of the subresource being requested.  This is a different resource, scoped to the parent resource, but it may have a different kind.\\n41: \\t// For instance, /pods has the resource \\\"pods\\\" and the kind \\\"Pod\\\", while /pods/foo/status has the resource \\\"pods\\\", the sub resource \\\"status\\\", and the kind \\\"Pod\\\"\\n42: \\t// (because status operates on pods). The binding resource for a pod though may be /pods/foo/binding, which has resource \\\"pods\\\", subresource \\\"binding\\\", and kind \\\"Binding\\\".\\n43: \\tGetSubresource() string\\n44: \\t// GetOperation is the operation being performed\\n45: \\tGetOperation() Operation\\n46: \\t// GetOperationOptions is the options for the operation being performed\\n47: \\tGetOperationOptions() runtime.Object\\n48: \\t// IsDryRun indicates that modifications will definitely not be persisted for this request. This is to prevent\\n49: \\t// admission controllers with side effects and a method of reconciliation from being overwhelmed.\\n50: \\t// However, a value of false for this does not mean that the modification will be persisted, because it\\n51: \\t// could still be rejected by a subsequent validation step.\\n52: \\tIsDryRun() bool\\n53: \\t// GetObject is the object from the incoming request prior to default values being applied\\n54: \\tGetObject() runtime.Object\\n55: \\t// GetOldObject is the existing object. Only populated for UPDATE and DELETE requests.\\n56: \\tGetOldObject() runtime.Object\\n57: \\t// GetKind is the type of object being manipulated.  For example: Pod\\n58: \\tGetKind() schema.GroupVersionKind\\n59: \\t// GetUserInfo is information about the requesting user\\n60: \\tGetUserInfo() user.Info\\n61: \\n62: \\t// AddAnnotation sets annotation according to key-value pair. ShutdownInitiated: KILL signal received\\n31: - AfterShutdownDelayDuration: shutdown delay duration has passed\\n32: - InFlightRequestsDrained: all in flight request(s) have been drained\\n33: - HasBeenReady is signaled when the readyz endpoint succeeds for the first time\\n34: \\n35: The following is a sequence of shutdown events that we expect to see with\\n36:   'ShutdownSendRetryAfter' = false:\\n37: \\n38: T0: ShutdownInitiated: KILL signal received\\n39: \\t- /readyz starts returning red\\n40:     - run pre shutdown hooks\\n41: \\n42: T0+70s: AfterShutdownDelayDuration: shutdown delay duration has passed\\n43: \\t- the default value of 'ShutdownDelayDuration' is '70s'\\n44: \\t- it's time to initiate shutdown of the HTTP Server, server.Shutdown is invoked\\n45: \\t- as a consequene, the Close function has is called for all listeners\\n46:  \\t- the HTTP Server stops listening immediately\\n47: \\t- any new request arriving on a new TCP socket is denied with\\n48:       a network error similar to 'connection refused'\\n49:     - the HTTP Server waits gracefully for existing requests to complete\\n50:       up to '60s' (dictated by ShutdownTimeout)\\n51: \\t- active long running requests will receive a GOAWAY.\\n52: \\n53: T0+70s: HTTPServerStoppedListening:\\n54: \\t- this event is signaled when the HTTP Server has stopped listening\\n55:       which is immediately after server.Shutdown has been invoked\\n56: \\n57: T0 + 70s + up-to 60s: InFlightRequestsDrained: existing in flight requests have been drained\\n58: \\t- long running requests are outside of this scope\\n59: \\t- up-to 60s: the default value of 'ShutdownTimeout' is 60s, this means that\\n60:       any request in flight has a hard timeout of 60s.\\n61: \\t- it's time to call 'Shutdown' on the audit events since all\\n62: \\t  in flight request(s) have drained.\\n63: \\n64: \\n65: The following is a sequence of shutdown events that we expect to see with\\n66:   'ShutdownSendRetryAfter' = true:\\n67: \\n68: T0: ShutdownInitiated: KILL signal received\\n69: \\t- /readyz starts returning red\\n70:     - run pre shutdown hooks\\n71: \\n72: T0+70s: AfterShutdownDelayDuration: shutdown delay duration has passed\\n73: \\t- the default value of 'ShutdownDelayDuration' is '70s'\\n74: \\t- the HTTP Server will continue to listen\\n75: \\t- the apiserver is not accepting new request(s)\\n76: \\t\\t- it includes new request(s) on a new or an existing TCP connection\\n77: \\t\\t- new request(s) arriving after this point are replied with a 429\\n78:       \\t  and the  response headers: 'Retry-After: 1` and 'Connection: close'\\n79: \\t- note: these new request(s) will not show up in audit logs\\n80: \\n81: T0 + 70s + up to 60s: InFlightRequestsDrained: existing in flight requests have been drained\\n82: \\t- long running requests are outside of this scope\\n83: \\t- up to 60s: the default value of 'ShutdownTimeout' is 60s, this means that\\n84:       any request in flight has a hard timeout of 60s.\\n85: \\t- server.Shutdown is called, the HTTP Server stops listening immediately\\n86:     - the HTTP Server waits gracefully for existing requests to complete\\n87:       up to '2s' (it's hard coded right now)\\n88: */\\n89: \\n90: // lifecycleSignal encapsulates a named apiserver event\\n91: type lifecycleSignal interface {\\n92: \\t// Signal signals the event, indicating that the event has occurred.\\n93: \\t// Signal is idempotent, once signaled the event stays signaled and\\n94: \\t// it immediately unblocks any goroutine waiting for this event.\\n95: \\tSignal()\\n96: \\n97: \\t// Signaled returns a channel that is closed when the underlying event\\n98: \\t// has been signaled. On a not found error, will either\n197: \t// return a zero object of the requested type, or an error, depending on 'opts.ignoreNotFound'.\n198: \t// Treats empty responses and nil response nodes exactly like a not found error.\n199: \t// The returned contents may be delayed, but it is guaranteed that they will\n200: \t// match 'opts.ResourceVersion' according 'opts.ResourceVersionMatch'.\n201: \tGet(ctx context.Context, key string, opts GetOptions, objPtr runtime.Object) error\n202: \n203: \t// GetList unmarshalls objects found at key into a *List api object (an object\n204: \t// that satisfies runtime.IsList definition).\n205: \t// If 'opts.Recursive' is false, 'key' is used as an exact match. If `opts.Recursive'\n206: \t// is true, 'key' is used as a prefix.\n207: \t// The returned contents may be delayed, but it is guaranteed that they will\n208: \t// match 'opts.ResourceVersion' according 'opts.ResourceVersionMatch'.\n209: \tGetList(ctx context.Context, key string, opts ListOptions, listObj runtime.Object) error\n210: \n211: \t// GuaranteedUpdate keeps calling 'tryUpdate()' to update key 'key' (of type 'destination')\n212: \t// retrying the update until success if there is index conflict.\n213: \t// Note that object passed to tryUpdate may change across invocations of tryUpdate() if\n214: \t// other writers are simultaneously updating it, so tryUpdate() needs to take into account\n215: \t// the current contents of the object when deciding how the update object should look.\n216: \t// If the key doesn't exist, it will return NotFound storage error if ignoreNotFound=false\n217: \t// else `destination` will be set to the zero value of it's type.\n218: \t// If the eventual successful invocation of `tryUpdate` returns an output with the same serialized\n219: \t// contents as the input, it won't perform any update, but instead set `destination` to an object with those\n220: \t// contents.\n221: \t// If 'cachedExistingObject' is non-nil, it can be used as a suggestion about the\n222: \t// current version of the object to avoid read operation from storage to get it.\n223: \t// However, the implementations have to retry in case suggestion is stale.\n224: \t//\n225: \t// Example:\n226: \t//\n227: \t// s := /* implementation of Interface */\n228: \t// err := s.GuaranteedUpdate(\n229: \t//     \"myKey\", &MyType{}, true, preconditions,\n230: \t//     func(input runtime.Object, res ResponseMeta) (runtime.Object, *uint64, error) {\n231: \t//       // Before each invocation of the user defined function, \"input\" is reset to\n232: \t//       // current contents for \"myKey\" in database.\n233: \t//       curr := input.(*MyType)  // Guaranteed to succeed.\n234: \t//\n235: \t//       // Make the modification\n236: \t//       curr.Counter++\n237: \t//\n238: \t//       // Return the modified object - return an error to stop iterating. Return\n239: \t//       // a uint64 to alter the TTL on the object, or nil to keep it the same value.\n240: \t//       return cur, nil, nil\n241: \t//    }, cachedExistingObject\n242: \t// )\n243: \tGuaranteedUpdate(\n244: \t\tctx context.Context, key string, destination runtime.Object, ignoreNotFound bool,\n245: \t\tpreconditions *Preconditions, tryUpdate UpdateFunc, cachedExistingObject runtime.Object) error\n246: \n247: \t// Stats returns storage stats.\n248: \tStats(ctx context.Context) (Stats, error)\n249: \n250: \t// ReadinessCheck checks if the storage is ready for accepting requests.\n251: \tReadinessCheck() error\n252: \n253: \t// RequestWatchProgress requests the a watch stream progress status be sent in the\n254: \t// watch response stream as soon as possible.\n255: \t// Used for monitor watch progress even if watching resources with no changes.\n256: \t//\n257: \t// If watch is lagging, progress status might:\n258: \t// * be pointing to stale resource version. Use etcd KV request to get linearizable resource version.\n259: \t// * not be delivered at all. Doing that with `/apis` as a webservice, means that it forcibly 404s (no defaulting allowed)\n56: \t// all requests which are not /apis or /apis/. Trying to\n57: \t// register for a pattern which includes everything behind it doesn't work because gorestful negotiates for verbs and content encoding\n58: \t// and all those things go crazy when gorestful really just needs to pass through.  In addition, openapi enforces unique verb constraints\n59: \t// which we don't fit into and it still muddies up swagger.  Trying to switch the webservices into a route doesn't work because the\n60: \t//  containing webservice faces all the same problems listed above.\n61: \t// This leads to the crazy thing done here.  Our mux does what we need, so we'll place it in front of gorestful.  It will introspect to\n62: \t// decide if the route is likely to be handled by gorestful and route there if needed.  Otherwise, it goes to NonGoRestfulMux mux in\n63: \t// order to handle \"normal\" paths and delegation. Hopefully no API consumers will ever have to deal with this level of detail. {
  "content": "# Kubernetes API Server Library: Architecture and Extension Guide\n\n## 1. Subsystem Purpose, Boundaries, and Dependencies\n\n### Purpose\n\n`k8s.io/apiserver` (`staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver`) is the **generic API server framework** that every Kubernetes API server is built upon. It provides all the machinery for serving Kubernetes-style REST APIs: TLS, authentication, authorization, admission control, watch caching, OpenAPI generation, graceful shutdown, and etcd storage integration. No business logic for specific resources lives here; it is purely plumbing.\n\nThe framework is used by three distinct server processes within the `kube-apiserver` binary\u2014the aggregation layer, the core API server, and the API extensions server\u2014as well as by any out-of-tree extension API server that embeds `RecommendedOptions`.\n\n### Boundaries\n\n**In scope:**\n- HTTP server lifecycle, handler-chain construction, and request routing\n- Authentication, authorization, and admission-control pipelines\n- Watch-cache layer in front of etcd\n- Registry/storage layer (generic CRUD operations, optimistic locking, dry-run)\n- API-group and resource registration / discovery\n- OpenAPI v2/v3 generation\n- Audit logging, metrics, tracing, health checks\n- Graceful startup and shutdown signaling\n\n**Out of scope:**\n- Concrete resource types (`Pod`, `Deployment`, etc.) \u2014 those live in `k8s.io/api` and `pkg/registry/{core,apps,...}` inside the main `kubernetes` repo\n- etcd itself \u2014 communicated with via `go.etcd.io/etcd/client/v3`\n- `kube-scheduler`, `kube-controller-manager`, `kubelet`\n\n### Upstream Dependencies\n\n| Dependency | Role |\n|---|---|\n| `k8s.io/apimachinery` | Type system (`runtime.Object`, `runtime.Scheme`, GroupVersionKind, serialization codecs, watch types) |\n| `k8s.io/api` | Standard API types consumed by built-in plugins |\n| `k8s.io/client-go` | In-cluster and loopback clients, informer framework, REST client |\n| `k8s.io/component-base` | Feature gates, metrics infrastructure, version information |\n| `k8s.io/kube-openapi` | OpenAPI spec generation and serving |\n| `go.etcd.io/etcd/client/v3` | etcd gRPC client |\n| `github.com/emicklei/go-restful/v3` | REST routing used inside `APIServerHandler` |\n| `sigs.k8s.io/structured-merge-diff` | Server-Side Apply field tracking |\n\n### Downstream Consumers\n\n| Consumer | What it does |\n|---|---|\n| `cmd/kube-apiserver` | Builds the three-server delegation chain |\n| `staging/src/k8s.io/kube-aggregator` | The aggregation-layer server; proxies to extension API servers |\n| `staging/src/k8s.io/apiextensions-apiserver` | CRD API server; dynamically installs REST storage for CRDs |\n| Any aggregated API server | Embeds `RecommendedOptions` and `GenericAPIServer` |\n\n---\n\n## 2. Key Components and Responsibility Split\n\n### 2.1 `Config` and `RecommendedConfig`\n\n**File:** `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/server/config.go`\n\n`Config` is the primary configuration struct for a `GenericAPIServer`. It is populated from command-line flags and environment before any server is instantiated. The most important fields drive request-processing policy:\n\n```go\ntype Config struct {\n    SecureServing    *SecureServingInfo       // TLS listener\n    Authentication   AuthenticationInfo       // Union authenticator\n    Authorization    AuthorizationInfo        // Union authorizer\n    AdmissionControl admission.Interface      // Admission chain\n    FlowControl      utilflowcontrol.Interface// APF; nil \u2192 simple in-flight limiter\n    BuildHandlerChainFunc func(http.Handler, *Config) http.Handler // replaceable\n    RESTOptionsGetter genericregistry.RESTOptionsGetter // factory for storage backends\n    ResourceTransformers storagevalue.ResourceTransformers // encryption\n    AuditBackend     audit.Backend\n    // ... timeouts, limits, feature gates\n}\n```\n\n`RecommendedConfig` embeds `Config` and adds a `SharedInformerFactory` and a `ClientConfig`, making it the natural base for extension API servers.\n\n`NewConfig()` sets all production defaults (`DefaultBuildHandlerChain`, `MaxRequestsInFlight: 400`, `MaxMutatingRequestsInFlight: 200`, `RequestTimeout: 60s`, `MaxRequestBodyBytes: 3 MiB`).\n\n**Extension hook:** Replace `BuildHandlerChainFunc` to insert custom middleware before or after the standard filters.\n\n### 2.2 `GenericAPIServer`\n\n**File:** `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/server/genericapiserver.go`\n\n`GenericAPIServer` is the runtime server struct. It holds an `APIServerHandler`, health-check registries, lifecycle signal channels, audit backend, admission control, and a pointer to the next `DelegationTarget` in the server chain.\n\nThe key lifecycle methods are:\n\n```\nPrepareRun()  \u2192 installs OpenAPI, health checks, statusz/flagz; returns preparedGenericAPIServer\nRunWithContext(ctx) \u2192 starts audit, HTTP server, post-start hooks; orchestrates graceful termination\n```\n\n`InstallAPIGroups(*APIGroupInfo...)` and `InstallLegacyAPIGroup(prefix, *APIGroupInfo)` are the entry points for registering API resources. They call the private `installAPIResources`, which drives the `APIInstaller`.\n\nThe `DelegationTarget` interface allows chaining: each server delegates unhandled requests to the next server in the chain, finally reaching an `emptyDelegate` that returns 404.\n\n### 2.3 `APIServerHandler`\n\n**File:** `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/server/handler.go`\n\nThe `APIServerHandler` is the HTTP handler tree for a single `GenericAPIServer`. It contains three layers:\n\n```\nFullHandlerChain   \u2190 the entire filter chain + director\n    \u2514\u2500 Director    \u2190 inspects URL to route to gorestful or mux\n         \u251c\u2500 GoRestfulContainer   \u2190 serves /apis/{group}/{version}/{resource}\n         \u2514\u2500 NonGoRestfulMux      \u2190 serves /healthz, /metrics, /openapi, etc.\n```\n\nThe `director` examines registered WebService root paths. If a path prefix matches a registered gorestful service (e.g., `/apis/apps`), the request goes to `GoRestfulContainer`; otherwise, it falls through to `NonGoRestfulMux`. This hybrid routing allows OpenAPI schema generation from gorestful while also supporting plain `http.Handler` endpoints.\n\n### 2.4 Authentication (`pkg/authentication`)\n\n**File:** `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/authentication/authenticator/interfaces.go`\n\nAuthentication is a union of pluggable `authenticator.Request` implementations:\n\n```go\ntype Request interface {\n    AuthenticateRequest(req *http.Request) (*Response, bool, error)\n}\n```\n\nThe union authenticator (in `pkg/authentication/request/union`) calls each plugin in order and accepts the first successful identification. Standard plugins include client-certificate, bearer-token, OIDC, service-account JWT, and bootstrap-token authenticators. When authentication fails, the request is handled by the `Unauthorized` error handler (which also writes an audit event).\n\n**Extension hook:** Implement `authenticator.Request` and add it to the union via `AuthenticationInfo.Authenticator`.\n\n### 2.5 Authorization (`pkg/authorization`)\n\n**File:** `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/authorization/authorizer/interfaces.go`\n\n```go\ntype Authorizer interface {\n    Authorize(ctx context.Context, a Attributes) (Decision, reason string, err error)\n}\n```\n\n`Decision` is one of `DecisionAllow`, `DecisionDeny`, or `DecisionNoOpinion`. The union authorizer (in `pkg/authorization/union`) passes the request through each authorizer until one returns Allow or Deny; NoOpinion means \"pass to the next\". Built-in implementations are RBAC, Node, Webhook, and ABAC.\n\n**Extension hook:** Implement `Authorizer` and register it in the union.\n\n### 2.6 Admission Control (`pkg/admission`)\n\n**Files:** `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/admission/interfaces.go`, `chain.go`, `reinvocation.go`\n\nAdmission is the last gatekeeping stage before a write hits storage, and it is the only stage where the request body has been fully decoded. Two interfaces exist:\n\n```go\ntype MutationInterface interface {\n    Handles(Operation) bool\n    Admit(ctx context.Context, a Attributes, o ObjectInterfaces) error\n}\n\ntype ValidationInterface interface {\n    Handles(Operation) bool\n    Validate(ctx context.Context, a Attributes, o ObjectInterfaces) error\n}\n```\n\nThe `chainAdmissionHandler` (`chain.go`) iterates all plugins in order and returns on the first error. A `reinvoker` wrapper (`reinvocation.go`) runs the mutation chain a second time if any mutating plugin set `ShouldReinvoke()` during its first pass\u2014this ensures that webhook mutations are seen by in-tree mutating plugins.\n\nBuilt-in plugins in `pkg/admission/plugin/` include:\n- `namespace/lifecycle` \u2013 enforces namespace existence\n- `resourcequota` \u2013 enforces quota\n- `cel` \u2013 CEL-based ValidatingAdmissionPolicy\n- `webhook` \u2013 mutating and validating webhook dispatchers\n- `policy` \u2013 Pod Security admission (PSA)\n\n**Extension hook:** Implement `MutationInterface` or `ValidationInterface`, register with `admission.RegisterPlugin()`, then enable via `--enable-admission-plugins`.\n\n### 2.7 Endpoints Layer (`pkg/endpoints`)\n\n**File:** `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/endpoints/installer.go`\n\nThe `APIInstaller` walks a `VersionedResourcesStorageMap` and, for each resource, reflects on which `rest.*` sub-interfaces the storage object implements (`Getter`, `Lister`, `Watcher`, `Creater`, `Updater`, `Deleter`, etc.) and registers corresponding HTTP routes in the `GoRestfulContainer`.\n\n```go\ntype APIInstaller struct {\n    group             *APIGroupVersion\n    prefix            string\n    minRequestTimeout time.Duration\n}\n```\n\nIt builds `action` structs (verb, path, parameters) and delegates to concrete handlers in `pkg/endpoints/handlers/` (e.g., `handlers.GetResource`, `handlers.CreateResource`, `handlers.UpdateResource`).\n\n### 2.8 Registry Layer (`pkg/registry/generic/registry`)\n\n**File:** `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/registry/generic/registry/store.go`\n\n`Store` is the generic CRUD implementation shared by all built-in resources. It wires together:\n\n- **Strategy objects** (`CreateStrategy`, `UpdateStrategy`, `DeleteStrategy`) that contain resource-specific validation and mutation logic\n- A `DryRunnableStorage` for dry-run support\n- Lifecycle hooks: `BeginCreate`/`AfterCreate`, `BeginUpdate`/`AfterUpdate`, `AfterDelete`\n\nThe strategy pattern separates generic transport semantics (conflict detection, etcd key construction, serialization) from resource-specific business logic. Resources embed `Store` and provide their own strategy.\n\n### 2.9 Storage Layer (`pkg/storage`)\n\n**File:** `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/storage/interfaces.go`\n\nThe `storage.Interface` is the lowest-level storage abstraction:\n\n```go\ntype Interface interface {\n    Create(ctx, key, obj, out, ttl) error\n    Delete(ctx, key, out, preconditions, validate, cachedObj, opts) error\n    Watch(ctx, key, opts) (watch.Interface, error)\n    Get(ctx, key, opts, objPtr) error\n    GetList(ctx, key, opts, listObj) error\n    GuaranteedUpdate(ctx, key, destination, ignoreNotFound, preconditions, tryUpdate, cachedObj) error\n    // ...\n}\n```\n\nThe concrete etcd3 implementation lives in `pkg/storage/etcd3/store.go`. It serializes objects to protobuf (via the codec), applies any configured `Transformer` (encryption), stores them under a path like `/registry/{group}/{resource}/{namespace}/{name}`, and maps etcd's `mod_revision` directly to Kubernetes `resourceVersion`.\n\n**Transformer abstraction** (`pkg/storage/value/transformer.go`):\n\n```go\ntype Transformer interface {\n    TransformFromStorage(ctx, data, dataCtx) (out []byte, stale bool, err error)\n    TransformToStorage(ctx, data, dataCtx) (out []byte, err error)\n}\n```\n\nThis is the pluggable encryption-at-rest hook used by KMS and AES-CBC/GCM providers.\n\n### 2.10 Watch Cache (`pkg/storage/cacher`)\n\n**File:** `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/storage/cacher/cacher.go`\n\n`Cacher` wraps `storage.Interface` and implements the same interface. It maintains a per-resource in-memory `WatchCache` that is populated by a single etcd watch stream. All client `Watch` and most `List` requests are served from this cache, dramatically reducing etcd load.\n\nThe `Cacher` tracks registered watchers in two maps:\n- `allWatchers` \u2013 watchers not using an indexed field\n- `valueWatchers` \u2013 watchers filtering by an indexed field (e.g., `spec.nodeName`)\n\nBookmark events are used to keep `ResourceVersion` from becoming stale without requiring expensive relists.\n\n---\n\n## 3. End-to-End Request Flow\n\n### 3.1 Server Chain Delegation\n\nA request to `kube-apiserver` first reaches the **Aggregator Server**. If no `APIService` object claims the path, the aggregator calls `delegationTarget.ServeHTTP`, which leads to the **Kube API Server** (core APIs). If the path is not a core API, control falls to the **API Extensions Server** (CRDs). If none handle it, the final `emptyDelegate` returns 404.\n\nThis is implemented via the `DelegationTarget` interface:\n\n```go\ntype DelegationTarget interface {\n    UnprotectedHandler() http.Handler\n    NextDelegate() DelegationTarget\n    PrepareRun() preparedGenericAPIServer\n    // ...\n}\n```\n\n### 3.2 Handler Chain (Inside a Single Server)\n\n`DefaultBuildHandlerChain` (in `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/server/config.go:1028`) constructs filters as a stack. Because Go's `http.Handler` wrapping works outside-in, the order of wrapping is the reverse of execution order. The final execution sequence for a request is:\n\n```\n1.  WithPanicRecovery        \u2013 catches panics, writes 500\n2.  WithAuditInit            \u2013 initializes audit context\n3.  WithRequestInfo          \u2013 parses URL into RequestInfo (verb, resource, name, ...)\n4.  WithMuxAndDiscoveryComplete \u2013 returns 503 until all paths registered\n5.  WithRequestReceivedTimestamp\n6.  WithLatencyTrackers\n7.  WithRoutine (optional)   \u2013 dispatches to goroutine (APIServingWithRoutine feature)\n8.  WithHTTPLogging\n9.  WithRetryAfter (optional)\n10. WithHSTS\n11. WithCacheControl         \u2013 sets Cache-Control: no-store on API responses\n12. WithProbabilisticGoaway (optional)\n13. WithWatchTerminationDuringShutdown (optional)\n14. WithWaitGroup            \u2013 tracks in-flight requests for graceful shutdown\n15. WithRequestDeadline      \u2013 sets context deadline from RequestTimeout\n16. WithTimeoutForNonLongRunningRequests\n17. WithWarningRecorder\n18. WithCORS\n19. WithAuthentication       \u2013 identifies the user; 401 on failure\n20. WithTracing (optional)   \u2013 OpenTelemetry span\n21. WithAudit                \u2013 logs pre/post audit events\n22. WithImpersonation        \u2013 processes Impersonate-* headers (re-checks authz)\n23. WithPriorityAndFairness  \u2013 classifies into FlowSchema/PriorityLevel, queues or rejects\n    OR WithMaxInFlightLimit  \u2013 legacy simple counter when APF is disabled\n24. WithAuthorization        \u2013 checks if user can perform the action; 403 on denial\n25. REST endpoint handler    \u2013 dispatched by APIInstaller/GoRestfulContainer\n```\n\nNote that the **request body is not decoded** until step 25. Authentication (step 19) and authorization (step 24) operate only on request metadata (URL, verb, user identity), which is critical for security: a malformed or oversized body cannot be used to exploit deserializers before the caller is verified.\n\n### 3.3 API Group Registration\n\n1. **Define types** in Go structs, annotated for `deepcopy-gen`, `conversion-gen`, `defaulter-gen`, and `openapi-gen`.\n2. **Create an `APIGroupInfo`** with a populated `runtime.Scheme` (GVK\u2192type mappings, conversion, defaulting) and a `VersionedResourcesStorageMap`.\n3. **Call `InstallAPIGroups`** on the `GenericAPIServer`. This calls `installAPIResources`, which creates an `APIGroupVersion` and calls `InstallREST` on the `GoRestfulContainer`.\n4. **`APIInstaller.Install()`** reflects on each `rest.Storage` implementor to determine which HTTP verbs to register, creates go-restful `WebService` objects, and connects them to handler functions.\n\n### 3.4 Read Path (GET / LIST)\n\n```\nClient GET /apis/apps/v1/namespaces/default/deployments/my-deploy\n  \u2514\u2500 REST handler (getResource)\n       \u2514\u2500 Store.Get()\n            \u2514\u2500 Cacher.Get()      \u2190 served from in-memory watch cache (if cache is fresh)\n                 OR\n                 etcd3.store.Get() \u2190 linearizable read from etcd (when cache is stale or bypassed)\n```\n\nLIST with a label/field selector may still be served from the cache via the `WatchCache.GetList()` path. Pagination (continue tokens) is handled by the etcd3 store using etcd range queries.\n\n### 3.5 Write Path (CREATE / UPDATE / DELETE)\n\n```\nClient POST /apis/apps/v1/namespaces/default/deployments\n  \u2514\u2500 REST handler (createResource)\n       \u251c\u2500 Decode body \u2192 runtime.Object\n       \u251c\u2500 Admission (Mutate all plugins \u2192 then Validate all plugins)\n       \u251c\u2500 Strategy.PrepareForCreate() \u2192 normalize, set defaults\n       \u2514\u2500 Store.Create()\n            \u2514\u2500 Cacher.Create()\n                 \u2514\u2500 etcd3.store.Create() \u2192 atomic PUT to etcd (fails if key exists)\n```\n\nFor UPDATE, `GuaranteedUpdate` is used: the etcd3 store performs a compare-and-swap loop using the etcd `mod_revision` as the optimistic lock. If the version mismatches (concurrent write), it re-reads and retries `tryUpdate`. The `Store`'s `Update()` handler surfaces this to the client as a `409 Conflict` when the client's `resourceVersion` does not match.\n\n---\n\n## 4. Failure Modes, Limits, and Design Tradeoffs\n\n### 4.1 In-Flight Request Limits\n\nTwo complementary mechanisms guard against overload:\n\n**Simple in-flight limiter** (default when APF is not enabled):\n- `MaxRequestsInFlight: 400` (non-mutating)\n- `MaxMutatingRequestsInFlight: 200` (mutating)\n- Requests over the limit receive 429 immediately with no queueing.\n\n**API Priority and Fairness (APF)** (`pkg/util/flowcontrol`):\n- Classifies requests into `FlowSchema` / `PriorityLevel` objects stored in etcd.\n- Each `PriorityLevel` gets a concurrency limit and a per-flow queue.\n- Provides fair sharing: a misbehaving controller cannot starve system components.\n- Work estimation (`NewWorkEstimator`) uses storage object counts and watch counts to estimate seat cost.\n- Risk: APF itself watches `FlowSchema` and `PriorityLevel` objects; if its informer falls behind, classification may be stale.\n\n**Design tradeoff:** APF adds latency for every request (queue check, seat accounting) but is essential in clusters with many controllers. The simple in-flight limiter is cheaper but unfair.\n\n### 4.2 Watch Cache Staleness and Fallback\n\nThe `Cacher` serves most watches and lists from its in-memory `WatchCache`. The cache is populated by a single long-running etcd watch. If the watch stream is disrupted:\n\n1. The cacher enters a `not ready` state.\n2. Incoming reads block until the cache is re-initialized (a fresh LIST + WATCH from etcd).\n3. If initialization exceeds `StorageInitializationTimeout` (default 1 minute), the server's readiness probe fails.\n\nIf a client requests a `resourceVersion` older than the watch cache's history window (controlled by `EventsHistoryWindow`, minimum `DefaultEventFreshDuration = ~75s`), the request falls through directly to etcd. This is expensive and signals the client is not keeping up.\n\n**Bookmark events** (`defaultBookmarkFrequency = 1 minute`) prevent the cache's resource version from aging: the cacher sends synthetic BOOKMARK events to watchers even when no actual object changes occur, allowing watchers to advance their acknowledged `resourceVersion` without a relist.\n\n### 4.3 Optimistic Concurrency and Conflict Resolution\n\nEvery object's `resourceVersion` maps directly to etcd's `mod_revision` for that key. On an update:\n- The client sends the object with the `resourceVersion` it last read.\n- The etcd3 store issues a compare-and-swap: `if mod_revision == expected, then set`.\n- If a concurrent writer already incremented the revision, the CAS fails and `GuaranteedUpdate` retries.\n- After a configurable number of retries, a `409 Conflict` is returned to the client with the message `\"the object has been modified; please apply your changes to the latest version and try again\"` (`OptimisticLockErrorMsg` in `store.go:262`).\n\n**Server-Side Apply (SSA)** provides an alternative: it uses `managedFields` metadata to track field ownership per manager. Conflicting field updates between different managers return a `409` indicating which manager owns the conflicting field, without requiring the client to own the full object.\n\n### 4.4 Request Size and Timeout Limits\n\n- `MaxRequestBodyBytes: 3 MiB` \u2014 requests exceeding this are rejected with 413 before reaching storage.\n- `JSONPatchMaxCopyBytes: 3 MiB` \u2014 limits total byte increase from JSON patch `copy` operations.\n- `RequestTimeout: 60s` \u2014 non-long-running requests are cancelled after this deadline.\n- Long-running requests (watches, exec, attach, port-forward) are exempt from the per-request timeout but are tracked separately.\n\n### 4.5 Admission Plugin Ordering and Reinvocation\n\nThe mutation chain is called first (all mutating plugins in order), followed by the validation chain. If a mutating plugin sets `ShouldReinvoke()` (e.g., a mutating webhook modified the object), the entire mutation chain is invoked a second time via the `reinvoker` wrapper (`reinvocation.go`). Only one reinvocation is performed. This means a plugin that always mutates and always sets `ShouldReinvoke` will be called exactly twice per request, not infinitely.\n\n**Design tradeoff:** Reinvocation ensures that webhook mutations are seen by in-tree mutating plugins and other webhooks configured with `reinvocationPolicy: IfNeeded`, but it doubles admission latency in the worst case.\n\n### 4.6 Graceful Shutdown Sequence\n\nDefined in `pkg/server/lifecycle_signals.go`. The sequence for a SIGTERM with default settings:\n\n```\nT+0:    SIGTERM received\n        \u2192 ShutdownInitiated signaled\n        \u2192 /readyz starts returning failure (load balancer detects this)\n        \u2192 PreShutdownHooks run (e.g., lease de-registration)\n\nT+70s:  AfterShutdownDelayDuration (ShutdownDelayDuration=70s elapsed)\n        \u2192 PreShutdownHooksStopped signaled (hooks finished)\n        \u2192 NotAcceptingNewRequest signaled\n        \u2192 HTTP server stops listening (or, with ShutdownSendRetryAfter, starts returning 429)\n\nT+130s: InFlightRequestsDrained (up to 60s ShutdownTimeout)\n        \u2192 Audit backend shutdown\n        \u2192 HTTPServerStoppedListening\n        \u2192 Process exits\n```\n\n**Operational implication:** A rolling update of `kube-apiserver` must allow at least `ShutdownDelayDuration + ShutdownTimeout` for each pod to drain before traffic is sent elsewhere. The default `ShutdownDelayDuration: 0` means load balancers may briefly send traffic to a terminating server unless explicitly configured.\n\n---\n\n## 5. Extension Points, Customization Hooks, and Associated Risks\n\n### 5.1 Replacing the Handler Chain\n\n```go\n// Config.BuildHandlerChainFunc\nconfig.BuildHandlerChainFunc = func(apiHandler http.Handler, c *server.Config) http.Handler {\n    handler := DefaultBuildHandlerChain(apiHandler, c)\n    return myLoggingMiddleware(handler)\n}\n```\n\n**Risk:** Removing standard filters (e.g., skipping authentication) has direct security consequences. Adding expensive middleware in the hot path degrades latency for all requests.\n\n### 5.2 Post-Start and Pre-Shutdown Hooks\n\n```go\nserver.AddPostStartHook(\"my-controller-start\", func(ctx server.PostStartHookContext) error {\n    go myController.Run(ctx.Context)\n    return nil\n})\nserver.AddPreShutdownHook(\"my-lease-release\", func() error {\n    return releaseLease()\n})\n```\n\n`PostStartHookFunc` receives a `PostStartHookContext` with a loopback client config and a `context.Context` that is cancelled when the server stops. Each hook runs in its own goroutine. If a hook returns a non-nil error, `klog.Fatalf` is called and the process dies.\n\n**Risk:** Panicking in a hook kills the server. Hooks that block indefinitely will hold the server in a not-ready state (each hook is exposed as a readiness check). Hooks registered after `RunPostStartHooks` has been called will fail with an error.\n\n### 5.3 Custom Admission Plugins\n\n```go\n// Register at startup before flag parsing\nadmission.RegisterPlugin(\"my-plugin\", func(config io.Reader) (admission.Interface, error) {\n    return NewMyPlugin(config), nil\n})\n```\n\nPlugins implement `MutationInterface` and/or `ValidationInterface`. To access Kubernetes objects or clients, implement `admission.PluginInitializer` and use the `ExtraAdmissionInitializers` hook in `RecommendedOptions`.\n\n**Risk:** A mutating plugin that modifies objects non-idempotently combined with reinvocation can produce unexpected results. A validating plugin that is too strict can break cluster operations if it inadvertently rejects system component requests.\n\n### 5.4 Custom Authenticators and Authorizers\n\nAdd a custom `authenticator.Request` to the union authenticator or a custom `authorizer.Authorizer` to the union authorizer. Both are composited before server start by populating `Config.Authentication.Authenticator` and `Config.Authorization.Authorizer`.\n\nFor extension API servers using `RecommendedOptions`, the delegating authentication and authorization options (`DelegatingAuthenticationOptions`, `DelegatingAuthorizationOptions`) forward authentication and authorization decisions to the main `kube-apiserver` via `SubjectAccessReview` and `TokenReview` API calls.\n\n**Risk:** A custom authorizer that always returns `DecisionAllow` eliminates access control. A custom authenticator that returns wrong user identity may elevate privileges.\n\n### 5.5 Custom REST Storage\n\nAny struct implementing `rest.Storage` (at minimum: `New() runtime.Object` and `Destroy()`) can be registered in an `APIGroupInfo.VersionedResourcesStorageMap`. To gain CRUD semantics, embed `genericregistry.Store` and provide a strategy.\n\nTo add a custom sub-resource (e.g., `/pods/log`), implement `rest.Connecter` (for streaming) or `rest.NamedCreater`, then register under a `subresource` key such as `pods/log` in the storage map.\n\n**Risk:** Embedding `Store` without a proper strategy can leak internal Go types through the API. Storage backends that are not idempotent under retry can cause data corruption with `GuaranteedUpdate`.\n\n### 5.6 Storage Encryption (Transformer)\n\n```go\n// Set in Config.ResourceTransformers\nconfig.ResourceTransformers = myKMSTransformerFactory\n```\n\nThe `value.Transformer` interface (`pkg/storage/value/transformer.go`) intercepts all reads and writes to etcd. The built-in KMS provider and AES-CBC/GCM providers are implementations.\n\n**Risk:** A faulty transformer that corrupts bytes will make objects unreadable. A transformer that fails silently (returns stale=false when data is stale) will prevent key rotation from being detected.\n\n### 5.7 API Aggregation (Aggregated API Servers)\n\nEmbed `RecommendedOptions` for plug-and-play configuration:\n\n```go\nopts := options.NewRecommendedOptions(\"/registry/mygroup.example.com\", codec)\nopts.ExtraAdmissionInitializers = func(c *server.RecommendedConfig) ([]admission.PluginInitializer, error) {\n    return []admission.PluginInitializer{myInitializer}, nil\n}\n```\n\nThe aggregated server registers an `APIService` object in the main cluster pointing to its `Service`. The aggregator server then proxies matching requests to it.\n\n**Risk:** Aggregated servers must handle their own TLS (or use insecure service networking with the aggregator performing TLS termination). A misconfigured `APIService` with a wrong `caBundle` causes all requests to that API group to fail with TLS errors.\n\n---\n\n## 6. Operational Implications\n\n### 6.1 Performance\n\n**Watch cache is the critical performance path.** Without the watch cache, every `LIST` and `WATCH` call from every controller would hit etcd directly. With a cluster of 500 nodes, that can mean thousands of open watches on the same resource. The cache serializes all etcd traffic for a given resource into a single etcd watch stream, fan-out happening entirely in-process.\n\nWatch fan-out uses the `indexedWatchers` map: if a watcher is filtering by an indexed field (e.g., `spec.nodeName=node-1`), it is placed in `valueWatchers[node-1]` and only receives events from the cacher's dispatch loop when the indexed value matches, without examining every other watcher. This reduces per-event CPU cost for large clusters.\n\n**Admission webhook latency** accumulates across all registered webhooks, since they are called sequentially. Each webhook call involves a network round-trip. Clustering webhooks behind a co-located sidecar (or using CEL-based `ValidatingAdmissionPolicy`, which runs in-process) avoids the network hop.\n\n**APF work estimation** (`pkg/util/flowcontrol/request`) uses `StorageObjectCountTracker.Get` to estimate list request cost as proportional to the number of objects in storage, and it tracks the number of interested watch watchers. Both are approximations; the work estimator can under- or over-estimate, leading to either wasted capacity or unfair prioritization.\n\n### 6.2 Reliability\n\n**etcd is the single point of persistence.** All apiserver replicas share the same etcd cluster. A full etcd outage stops all writes and prevents the watch cache from refreshing. Reads may still be served from the cache for the duration of the history window.\n\n**Panic recovery** in the handler chain (`WithPanicRecovery`) prevents a panicking request handler from killing the process, but the panic is logged and a 500 is returned. Repeated panics from the same code path indicate a bug and should be treated as alerts.\n\n**Post-start hook health checks** block the `/readyz` endpoint until each hook reports completion. If a hook never completes (e.g., because it is waiting for a CRD that does not yet exist), the server will never become ready, causing a deployment rollout to hang. The `LivezGracePeriod` provides a window during which `/livez` returns healthy even if post-start hooks are incomplete.\n\n### 6.3 Maintainability\n\n**The hub-and-spoke conversion model** (`runtime.Scheme`): objects are converted to/from an internal hub version when moving between API versions. Adding a new external version requires only a conversion function to/from the internal type, not N\u00d7M conversions between all pairs of versions. However, the internal type must be kept as a superset of all external types, which can lead to internal types accumulating fields that have been removed from all external versions.\n\n**Feature gates** (`pkg/util/feature`) allow new behaviors to be introduced behind a flag without forking the binary. Gates transition through alpha \u2192 beta \u2192 GA \u2192 removed over multiple releases. Admission plugins and handler chain modifications gated on a feature can be enabled/disabled at runtime with a flag restart. Over-reliance on feature gates creates configuration complexity; gates that are never cleaned up accumulate as technical debt.\n\n**Code generation dependency:** `deepcopy-gen`, `conversion-gen`, `defaulter-gen`, `openapi-gen` must be re-run whenever types change. Generated files (`zz_generated.deepcopy.go`, `zz_generated.openapi.go`, etc.) are committed to the repository. Out-of-date generated files will be caught by CI but can be confusing to diagnose.\n\n---\n\n## 7. File and Directory Map\n\n```\nstaging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/\n\u251c\u2500\u2500 ARCHITECTURE.md                     \u2190 Official architecture overview (start here)\n\u251c\u2500\u2500 pkg/\n\u2502   \u251c\u2500\u2500 server/\n\u2502   \u2502   \u251c\u2500\u2500 config.go                   \u2190 Config, RecommendedConfig, DefaultBuildHandlerChain\n\u2502   \u2502   \u251c\u2500\u2500 genericapiserver.go         \u2190 GenericAPIServer, APIGroupInfo, DelegationTarget\n\u2502   \u2502   \u251c\u2500\u2500 handler.go                  \u2190 APIServerHandler, Director, GoRestful/NonGoRestful split\n\u2502   \u2502   \u251c\u2500\u2500 hooks.go                    \u2190 PostStartHookFunc, AddPostStartHook, RunPostStartHooks\n\u2502   \u2502   \u251c\u2500\u2500
